      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Sinegal" title="Sinegal">Sinegal</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country. For the river, see <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Senegal</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Senegal.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/En-us-Senegal.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Senegal.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> French: <i lang="fr">Sénégal</i>; <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">Wolof</a>: <i>Senegaal</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Senegal</b> (French: <i lang="fr">République du Sénégal</i>; <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">Wolof</a>: <i>Réewum Senegaal</i>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Senegal is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mauritania%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Mauritania–Senegal border">the north</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mali%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Mali–Senegal border">the east</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guinea%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Guinea–Senegal border">the southeast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Guinea-Bissau–Senegal border">the southwest</a>. Senegal nearly <a href="/wiki/Gambia%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Gambia–Senegal border">surrounds</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">The Gambia</a>, a country occupying a narrow sliver of land along the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Gambia_River" title="Gambia River">Gambia River</a>, which separates Senegal's southern region of <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">Casamance</a> from the rest of the country. Senegal also shares a maritime border with <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Senegal's economic and political capital is <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential republic</a> and is the western-most country in <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">Afro-Eurasia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It owes its name to the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a>, which borders it to the east and north. Senegal covers a land area of almost 197,000 square kilometres (76,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and has a population of around 16 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> The state was formed as part of the independence of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> from French colonial rule. Because of this history, the official language is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Like other post-colonial African states, the country includes a wide <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Senegal" title="Demographics of Senegal">mix of ethnic and linguistic communities</a>, with the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Wolof_people" title="Wolof people">Wolof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">Serer people</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">Wolof</a> and French languages acting as <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua francas</a>. </p>
      <p>Senegal is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Heavily_indebted_poor_countries" title="Heavily indebted poor countries">heavily indebted poor country</a>, with a relatively low <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Human Development Index</a>. Most of the population is on the coast and works <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Senegal" title="Agriculture in Senegal">in agriculture or other food industries</a>. Other major industries include mining, tourism and services.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The climate is typically <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a>, though there is a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">rainy season</a>. </p>
      <p>Senegal is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS), and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">Community of Sahel-Saharan States</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>"Senegal" probably derives from a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> transliteration of the name of the <a href="/wiki/Zenaga_language" title="Zenaga language">Zenaga</a>, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Sanhaja" title="Sanhaja">Sanhaja</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fass_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fass-17">[17]</a></sup> or else a combination of the supreme deity in <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion" title="Serer religion">Serer religion</a> (<i>Rog Sene</i>) and <i>o gal</i> meaning <i>body of water</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Serer_language" title="Serer language">Serer language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Emery2013_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Emery2013-18">[18]</a></sup> Alternatively, the name could derive from the <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">Wolof</a> phrase <i>Sunuu Gaal</i>, which means "our boat."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Senegal" title="History of Senegal">History of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_and_pre-colonial_eras">Early and pre-colonial eras</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early and pre-colonial eras">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Archaeological findings throughout the area indicate that Senegal was inhabited in prehistoric times and has been continuously occupied by various ethnic groups. Some kingdoms were created around the 7th century: <a href="/wiki/Takrur" title="Takrur">Takrur</a> in the 9th century, Namandiru and the <a href="/wiki/Jolof_Empire" title="Jolof Empire">Jolof Empire</a> during the 13th and 14th centuries. Eastern Senegal was once part of the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a>. </p>
      <p>Islam was introduced through <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">Toucouleur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">Soninke</a> contact with the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid dynasty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>, who in turn propagated it with the help of the Almoravids and Toucouleur allies. This movement faced resistance from ethnicities of traditional religions, the Serers in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 13th and 14th centuries, the area came under the influence of the empires to the east; the Jolof Empire of Senegal was also founded during this time. In the Senegambia region, between 1300 and 1900, close to one-third of the population was <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">enslaved</a>, typically as a result of being taken captive in warfare.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 14th century the Jolof Empire grew more powerful, having united <a href="/wiki/Cayor" title="Cayor">Cayor</a> and the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Baol" title="Baol">Baol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sine" title="Kingdom of Sine">Siné</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saloum" title="Saloum">Saloum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waalo" title="Waalo">Waalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futa_Tooro" title="Futa Tooro">Futa Tooro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bambouk" title="Bambouk">Bambouk</a>, or much of present-day West Africa. The empire was a voluntary confederacy of various states rather than being built on military conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-charles_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charles-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The empire was founded by Ndiadiane Ndiaye, a part <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">Serer</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and part <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">Toucouleur</a>, who was able to form a coalition with many ethnicities, but collapsed around 1549 with the defeat and killing of Lele Fouli Fak by Amari Ngone Sobel Fall. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Senegambia_(Dutch_West_India_Company)" title="Senegambia (Dutch West India Company)">Senegambia (Dutch West India Company)</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Senegal" title="French conquest of Senegal">French conquest of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg/220px-AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg/330px-AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg/440px-AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2004"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AMH-8133-KB_Floor_plan_of_the_fort_on_Goeree.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> was the first European power to colonize Senegal, beginning with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Dinis_Dias" title="Dinis Dias">Dinis Dias</a> in 1444 at <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée Island</a> and ending in 1888, when the Portuguese gave <a href="/wiki/Ziguinchor" title="Ziguinchor">Ziguinchor</a> to the French.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the mid-15th century, the Portuguese landed on the Senegal coastline, followed by traders representing other countries, including the French.<sup id="cite_ref-ross_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ross-27">[27]</a></sup> Various European powers — Portugal, the Netherlands, and Great Britain — competed for trade in the area from the 15th century onward. </p>
      <p>In 1677, France gained control of what had become a minor departure point in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>: the island of <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée</a> next to modern Dakar, used as a base to purchase slaves from the warring chiefdoms on the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-h-net.org_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-h-net.org-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/170px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/255px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/340px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2531" data-file-height="3585"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>French slave traders in <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée</a>, 18th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>European missionaries introduced Christianity to Senegal and the <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">Casamance</a> in the 19th century. It was only in the 1850s that the French began to expand onto the Senegalese mainland, after they abolished slavery and began promoting an <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolitionism in France">abolitionist</a> doctrine,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> adding native kingdoms like the Waalo, Cayor, Baol, and Jolof Empire. French colonists progressively invaded and took over all the kingdoms, except Siné and Saloum, under Governor <a href="/wiki/Louis_Faidherbe" title="Louis Faidherbe">Louis Faidherbe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-charles_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charles-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Yoro_Dyao" title="Yoro Dyao">Yoro Dyao</a> was in command of the canton of Foss-Galodjina and was set over Wâlo (Ouâlo) by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Faidherbe" title="Louis Faidherbe">Louis Faidherbe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Royal_II_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Royal_II-32">[32]</a></sup> where he served as a chief from 1861 to 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolof_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolof-33">[33]</a></sup> Senegalese resistance to the French expansion and curtailing of their lucrative slave trade was led in part by <a href="/wiki/Lat-Dior" class="mw-redirect" title="Lat-Dior">Lat-Dior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damel" title="Damel">Damel</a> of Cayor, and <a href="/wiki/Maad_a_Sinig_Kumba_Ndoffene_Famak_Joof" title="Maad a Sinig Kumba Ndoffene Famak Joof">Maad a Sinig Kumba Ndoffene Famak Joof</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maad_a_Sinig" title="Maad a Sinig">Maad a Sinig</a> of Siné, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Logand%C3%A8me" title="Battle of Logandème">Battle of Logandème</a>. In 1915, over 300 Senegalese came under Australian command, ahead of the taking of Damascus by Australians, before the expected arrival of the famed Lawrence of Arabia. French and British diplomacy in the area were thrown into disarray. </p>
      <p>On 25 November 1958, Senegal became an autonomous republic within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1960)">Independence (1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence (1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 4 April 1959 Senegal and the <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French Sudan</a> merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Federation" title="Mali Federation">Mali Federation</a>, which became fully independent on 20 June 1960, as a result of a transfer of power agreement signed with France on 4 April 1960. Due to internal political difficulties, the Federation broke up on 20 August, when Senegal and French Sudan (renamed the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>) each proclaimed independence. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">Léopold Sédar Senghor</a> was Senegal's first president in September 1960. Senghor was a very well-read man, educated in France. He was a poet and philosopher who personally drafted the Senegalese national anthem, "Pincez tous vos koras, frappez les balafons" (English: <i>"Strum all thy koras, strike the balafons")</i>. Pro-African, he advocated a brand of African socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/220px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/330px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/440px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="289"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Colonial <a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis,_Senegal" title="Saint-Louis, Senegal">Saint Louis</a> c. 1900. Europeans and Africans on the Rue Lebon.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1980, President Senghor decided to retire from politics. The next year, he transferred power in 1981 to his hand-picked successor, <a href="/wiki/Abdou_Diouf" title="Abdou Diouf">Abdou Diouf</a>. Former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Mamadou_Dia" title="Mamadou Dia">Mamadou Dia</a>, who was Senghor's rival, ran for election in 1983 against Diouf, but lost. Senghor moved to France, where he died at the age of 95. </p>
      <p>In the 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Boubacar_Lam" class="mw-redirect" title="Boubacar Lam">Boubacar Lam</a> discovered Senegalese oral history that was initially compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">Tuculor</a> noble, <a href="/wiki/Yoro_Dy%C3%A2o" class="mw-redirect" title="Yoro Dyâo">Yoro Dyâo</a>, not long after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, which documented migrations into <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a>; ethnic groups, from the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a>, retained traditions of having an eastern origin.<sup id="cite_ref-AfrAm_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AfrAm-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal joined with <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">The Gambia</a> to form the nominal <a href="/wiki/Senegambia_Confederation" title="Senegambia Confederation">Senegambia Confederation</a> on 1 February 1982. However, the union was dissolved in 1989. Despite peace talks, a southern separatist group (<a href="/wiki/Movement_of_Democratic_Forces_of_Casamance" title="Movement of Democratic Forces of Casamance">Movement of Democratic Forces of Casamance</a> or MFDC) in the <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">Casamance</a> region has clashed sporadically with government forces since 1982 in the <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">Casamance conflict</a>. In the early 21st century, violence has subsided and President <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">Macky Sall</a> held talks with rebels in Rome in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Abdou Diouf was president between 1981 and 2000. He encouraged broader political participation, reduced government involvement in the economy, and widened Senegal's diplomatic engagements, particularly with other developing nations. Domestic politics on occasion spilled over into street violence, border tensions, and a violent separatist movement in the southern region of the Casamance. Nevertheless, Senegal's commitment to democracy and human rights strengthened. Abdou Diouf served four terms as president. </p>
      <p>In the presidential election of 1999, opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">Abdoulaye Wade</a> defeated Diouf in an election deemed free and fair by international observers. Senegal experienced its second <a href="/wiki/Peaceful_transition_of_power" title="Peaceful transition of power">peaceful transition of power</a>, and its first from one political party to another. On 30 December 2004 President Wade announced that he would sign a peace treaty with the separatist group in the Casamance region. This, however, has yet to be implemented. There was a round of talks in 2005, but the results have not yet yielded a resolution. </p>
      <p>In March 2012, the incumbent president Abdoulaye Wade lost the <a href="/wiki/2012_Senegalese_presidential_election" title="2012 Senegalese presidential election">presidential election</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">Macky Sall</a> was elected as the new President of Senegal.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> President Macky Sall was re-elected in <a href="/wiki/2019_Senegalese_presidential_election" title="2019 Senegalese presidential election">2019 elections</a>. The presidential term was reduced from seven years to five.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Senegal" title="Politics of Senegal">Politics of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg/170px-Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg/255px-Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg/340px-Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="868" data-file-height="1280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Macky_Sall_-_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">Macky Sall</a>, President of Senegal (2012–present)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/170px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/255px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/340px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="801"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">Abdoulaye Wade</a>, President of Senegal (2000–2012)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Senegal is a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> with a presidency; the president is <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Senegal" title="Elections in Senegal">elected</a> every five years as of 2016, previously being seven years from independence to 2001, five years from 2001 to 2008, and 7 years again from 2008 to 2016, by adult voters. The first president, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">Léopold Sédar Senghor</a>, was a poet and writer, and was the first African elected to the <i>Académie française</i>. Senegal's second president, <a href="/wiki/Abdou_Diouf" title="Abdou Diouf">Abdou Diouf</a>, later served as general secretary of the <i>Organisation de la Francophonie</i>. The third president was <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">Abdoulaye Wade</a>, a lawyer. The current president is <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">Macky Sall</a>, elected in March 2012 and reelected in February <a href="/wiki/2019_in_Senegal" title="2019 in Senegal">2019</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal has more than 80 political parties. The <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> parliament consists of the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Senegal" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Senegal">National Assembly</a>, which has 150&nbsp;seats (a <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Senegal)" title="Senate (Senegal)">Senate</a> was in place from 1999 to 2001 and 2007 to 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> An independent judiciary also exists in Senegal. The nation's highest courts that deal with business issues are the constitutional council and the court of justice, members of which are named by the president. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Currently, Senegal has a quasi-democratic political culture, one of the more successful post-colonial democratic transitions in Africa. Local administrators are appointed and held accountable by the president. <a href="/wiki/Marabout" title="Marabout">Marabouts</a>, religious leaders of the various <a href="/wiki/Muslim_brotherhoods_of_Senegal" title="Muslim brotherhoods of Senegal">Muslim brotherhoods of Senegal</a>, have also exercised a strong political influence in the country especially during Wade's presidency. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> downgraded Senegal's status from "Free" to "Partially Free", based on increased centralisation of power in the executive. By 2014, it had recovered its Free status.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Senegal finished in 12th position on the <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ibrahim_index_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibrahim_index-42">[42]</a></sup> The Ibrahim Index is a comprehensive measure of African governance (limited to <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> until 2008), based on a number of different variables which reflect the success with which governments deliver essential political goods to their citizens. When the Northern African countries were added to the index in 2009, Senegal's 2008 position was retroactively downgraded to 15th place (with Tunisia, Egypt and Morocco placing themselves ahead of Senegal). As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Senegal's rank in the Ibrahim Index has decreased another point to 16 out of 52 African countries. </p>
      <p>On 22 February 2011, Senegal severed diplomatic ties with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, saying it supplied rebels with weapons which killed Senegalese troops in the <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">Casamance conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_presidential_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Senegalese presidential election, 2012">2012 presidential election</a> was controversial due to President Wade's candidacy, as the opposition argued he should not be considered eligible to run for the presidency again. Several youth opposition movements, including M23 and <a href="/wiki/Y%27en_a_Marre" title="Y'en a Marre">Y'en a Marre</a>, emerged in June 2011. In the end, Macky Sall of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_the_Republic_(Senegal)" title="Alliance for the Republic (Senegal)">Alliance for the Republic</a> won, and Wade conceded the election to Sall. This peaceful and democratic transition was hailed by many foreign observers, such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> as a show of "maturity". </p>
      <p>On 19 September 2012, lawmakers voted to do away with the Senate to save an estimated $15 million.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2017, the ruling party won a landslide victory in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Senegalese_parliamentary_election" title="2017 Senegalese parliamentary election">parliamentary election</a>. President Macky Sall's ruling coalition took 125 seats in the 165-seat National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In 2019 president Macky Sall easily won <a href="/wiki/2019_Senegalese_presidential_election" title="2019 Senegalese presidential election">re-election</a> in the first round.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Senegal" title="Regions of Senegal">Regions of Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Senegal" title="Departments of Senegal">Departments of Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Senegal" title="Arrondissements of Senegal">Arrondissements of Senegal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Senegal" title="Communes of Senegal">Communes of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal,_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/450px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="337" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/675px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/900px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1264" data-file-height="947"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal,_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Regions of Senegal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Senegal is subdivided into 14 regions,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> each administered by a <i>Conseil Régional</i> (Regional Council) elected by population weight at the <i>Arrondissement</i> level. The country is further subdivided by 45 <i>Départements</i>, 113 <i>Arrondissements</i> (neither of which have administrative function) and by <i>Collectivités Locales</i>, which elect administrative officers.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Regional capitals have the same name as their respective regions: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dakar_Region" title="Dakar Region">Dakar</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Diourbel_Region" title="Diourbel Region">Diourbel</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Fatick_Region" title="Fatick Region">Fatick</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Kaffrine_Region" title="Kaffrine Region">Kaffrine</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Kaolack_Region" title="Kaolack Region">Kaolack</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9dougou_Region" title="Kédougou Region">Kédougou</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Kolda_Region" title="Kolda Region">Kolda</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Louga_Region" title="Louga Region">Louga</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Matam_Region" title="Matam Region">Matam</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis_Region" title="Saint-Louis Region">Saint-Louis</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9dhiou_Region" title="Sédhiou Region">Sédhiou</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Tambacounda_Region" title="Tambacounda Region">Tambacounda</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Thi%C3%A8s_Region" title="Thiès Region">Thiès</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Ziguinchor_Region" title="Ziguinchor Region">Ziguinchor</a></li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Senegal" title="Foreign relations of Senegal">Foreign relations of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Senegal has a high profile in many international organizations and was a member of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> in 1988–89 and 2015–2016. It was elected to the <a href="/wiki/UN_Commission_on_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Commission on Human Rights">UN Commission on Human Rights</a> in 1997. Friendly to the West, especially to France and to the United States, Senegal also is a vigorous proponent of more assistance from developed countries to the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>. </p>
      <p>Senegal enjoys mostly cordial relations with its neighbors. In spite of clear progress on other fronts with <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> (border security, resource management, economic integration, etc.), an estimated 35,000 Mauritanian refugees (of the estimated 40,000 who were expelled from their home country in 1989) remain in Senegal.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal is part of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS). Integrated with the main bodies of the international community, Senegal is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU) and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">Community of Sahel-Saharan States</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor,_Senegal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/220px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/330px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/440px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4326" data-file-height="2865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor,_Senegal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Land mines were widely used in the <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">Casamance conflict</a> between separatist rebels and the central government.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Senegal" title="Armed Forces of Senegal">Armed Forces of Senegal</a> consist of about 17,000 personnel in the army, <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_Air_Force" title="Senegalese Air Force">air force</a>, navy, and gendarmerie. The Senegalese military force receives most of its training, equipment, and support from France and the United States. Germany also provides support, but on a smaller scale. </p>
      <p>Military noninterference in political affairs has contributed to Senegal's stability since independence. Senegal has participated in many international and regional peacekeeping missions. Most recently, in 2000, Senegal sent a battalion to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> to participate in <a href="/wiki/MONUC" class="mw-redirect" title="MONUC">MONUC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> peacekeeping mission, and agreed to deploy a United States-trained battalion to <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> to participate in <a href="/wiki/UNAMSIL" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAMSIL">UNAMSIL</a>, another UN peacekeeping mission. </p>
      <p>In 2015, Senegal participated in the Saudi Arabian-led <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">military intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Senegal is a secular state, as defined in its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Senegal" title="Constitution of Senegal">Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_of_Senegal_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_of_Senegal-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>To fight corruption, the government has created the National Anti-Corruption Office (OFNAC) and the Commission of Restitution and Recovery of Illegally Acquired Assets. According to Business Anti-Corruption Portal, President Sall created the OFNAC to replace the Commission Nationale de Lutte Contre la non Transparence, la Corruption et la Concussion (CNLCC). It is said that the OFNAC represents a more effective tool for fighting corruption than the CNLCC established under former President Wade.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The mission of OFNAC is to fight corruption, embezzlement of public funds and fraud. OFNAC has the power of self-referral (own-initiative investigation). OFNAC is composed of twelve members appointed by decree. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Senegal" title="LGBT rights in Senegal">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Senegal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> According to 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 96% of Senegalese believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-55">[55]</a></sup> LGBTQ community members in Senegal report a strong feeling of being unsafe.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Senegal" title="Geography of Senegal">Geography of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Senegal map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Casamance_landscape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/220px-Casamance_landscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/330px-Casamance_landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/440px-Casamance_landscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="583" data-file-height="389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Casamance_landscape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Landscape of <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">Casamance</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Senegal is located on the west of the African continent. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">12°</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_north" title="17th parallel north">17°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_west" title="11th meridian west">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_meridian_west" title="18th meridian west">18°W</a>. </p>
      <p>Senegal is externally bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> to the south; internally it almost completely surrounds <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">The Gambia</a>, namely on the north, east and south, except for Gambia's short Atlantic coastline. </p>
      <p>The Senegalese landscape consists mainly of the rolling sandy plains of the western <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> which rise to foothills in the southeast. Here is also found Senegal's highest point, an otherwise unnamed feature 2.7&nbsp;km southeast of <a href="/wiki/Nepen_Diakha" title="Nepen Diakha">Nepen Diakha</a> at 648&nbsp;m (2,126&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The northern border is formed by the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a>; other rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Gambia_River" title="Gambia River">Gambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Casamance_River" title="Casamance River">Casamance Rivers</a>. The capital Dakar lies on the <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">Cap-Vert</a> peninsula, the westernmost point of continental Africa. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands lie some 560 kilometres (350&nbsp;mi) off the Senegalese coast, but Cap-Vert ("Cape Green") is a maritime placemark, set at the foot of "Les Mammelles", a 105-metre (344&nbsp;ft) cliff resting at one end of the Cap-Vert peninsula onto which is settled Senegal's capital Dakar, and 1 kilometre (0.6&nbsp;mi) south of the "<a href="/wiki/Pointe_des_Almadies" title="Pointe des Almadies">Pointe des Almadies</a>", the westernmost point in Africa. </p>
      <p>Senegal contains four terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-58">[58]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.11/10, ranking it 56th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Senegal" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Senegal">Climate of Senegal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ngor_Beach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/220px-Ngor_Beach.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/330px-Ngor_Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/440px-Ngor_Beach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3475" data-file-height="2606"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ngor_Beach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach at <a href="/wiki/Ngor,_Dakar" title="Ngor, Dakar">N'Gor</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Senegal has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with pleasant heat throughout the year with well-defined dry and humid seasons that result from northeast winter winds and southwest summer winds. The dry season (December to April) is dominated by hot, dry, <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> wind.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> Dakar's annual rainfall of about 600&nbsp;mm (24&nbsp;in) occurs between June and October when maximum temperatures average 30&nbsp;°C (86.0&nbsp;°F) and minimums 24.2&nbsp;°C (75.6&nbsp;°F); December to February maximum temperatures average 25.7&nbsp;°C (78.3&nbsp;°F) and minimums 18&nbsp;°C (64.4&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Interior temperatures are higher than along the coast (for example, average daily temperatures in Kaolack and Tambacounda for May are 30&nbsp;°C (86.0&nbsp;°F) and 32.7&nbsp;°C (90.9&nbsp;°F) respectively, compared to Dakar's 23.2&nbsp;°C (73.8&nbsp;°F) ),<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and rainfall increases substantially farther south, exceeding 1,500&nbsp;mm (59.1&nbsp;in) annually in some areas. </p>
      <p>In Tambacounda in the far interior, particularly on the border of Mali where desert begins, temperatures can reach as high as 54&nbsp;°C (129.2&nbsp;°F). The northernmost part of the country has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a>, the central part has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> and the southernmost part has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wet_and_dry_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical wet and dry climate">tropical wet and dry climate</a>. Senegal is mainly a sunny and dry country. </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Econimpact2c.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Econimpact2c.png/300px-Econimpact2c.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Econimpact2c.png/450px-Econimpact2c.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Econimpact2c.png/600px-Econimpact2c.png 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Econimpact2c.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Economic impact of 2°C in Senegal
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Senegal" title="Climate change in Senegal">Climate change in Senegal</a> will have wide reaching impacts on many aspects of life in Senegal. <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> will cause an increase in average temperatures over west Africa by between 1.5 and 4 °C (3 °F and 7 °F) by mid-century, relative to 1986–2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:7_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:7-62">[62]</a></sup> Projections of rainfall indicate an overall decrease in rainfall and an increase in intense mega-storm events over the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:8_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:8-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:9_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:9-64">[64]</a></sup> The sea level is expected to rise faster in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> than the global average.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:10_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:10-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:11_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:11-66">[66]</a></sup> Although Senegal is currently not a major contributor to global <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>, it is one of the most vulnerable countries to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:2_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:2-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:12_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:12-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> Extreme <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> is impacting <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, and causing food and job insecurity. More than 70% of the <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> is employed in the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Senegal" title="Agriculture in Senegal">agricultural sector</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">Sea level rise</a> and resulting <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">coastal erosion</a> is expected to cause damage to coastal infrastructure and displace a large percentage of the population living in <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coastal</a> areas. Climate change also has the potential to increase <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">land degradation</a> that will likely increase <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a> in eastern Senegal, leading to an expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Senegal_:1-69">[69]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Senegal" title="Economy of Senegal">Economy of Senegal</a>
      </div>
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="excerpt">
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg/220px-Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg/330px-Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg/440px-Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Dakar-Ind%C3%A9pendance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Dakar, Senegal's <i>place de l'Indépendance</i>: a center of government, banking and trade. In the background is the commercial port and the tourist area, <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée</a> island.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> 
        <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Senegal" title="Economy of Senegal">economy of Senegal</a> is driven by mining, construction, tourism, fishing and agriculture, which are the main sources of employment in rural areas, despite abundant natural resources in iron, zircon, gas, gold, phosphates, and numerous oil discoveries recently. Senegal's economy gains most of its foreign exchange from <a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_phosphate" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock phosphate">phosphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">groundnuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourist_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourist industry">tourism</a>, and services. As one of the dominant parts of the economy, the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> sector of Senegal is highly vulnerable to environmental conditions, such as variations in rainfall <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Senegal" title="Climate change in Senegal">and climate change</a>, and changes in world <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodity prices</a>. </p>
        <p>The former capital of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a>, is also home to banks and other institutions which serve all of Francophone West Africa, and is a hub for shipping and transport in the region. </p>
        <p>Senegal also has one of the best developed tourist industries in Africa. Senegal's economy depends on foreign assistance. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>. </p> The main obstacles to the economic development of the country are among others a great corruption with inefficient justice, very slow administrative formalities, a failing education sector.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_trade">Industry and trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Industry and trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/350px-Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="350" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/525px-Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg/700px-Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_Exports_Treemap_2017.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Senegal's exports in 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main industries include <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, cement, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_fertilizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial fertilizer">artificial fertilizer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Refining" title="Refining">refining</a> imported petroleum, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Senegal" title="Tourism in Senegal">tourism</a>. Exports include fish, chemicals, cotton, fabrics, <a href="/wiki/Bambara_groundnut" class="mw-redirect" title="Bambara groundnut">groundnuts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Calcium_phosphate" title="Calcium phosphate">calcium phosphate</a>. The principal foreign market is India with 26.7% of exports (as of 1998). Other foreign markets include the United States, Italy and the United Kingdom. </p>
      <p>As a member of the <a href="/wiki/West_African_Economic_and_Monetary_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="West African Economic and Monetary Union">West African Economic and Monetary Union</a> (WAEMU), Senegal is working toward greater regional integration with a unified external <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariff</a>. Senegal is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal achieved full Internet connectivity in 1996, creating a mini-boom in information technology-based services. Private activity now accounts for 82 percent of its GDP. On the negative side, Senegal faces deep-seated urban problems of chronic high unemployment, <a href="/wiki/Income_disparity" class="mw-redirect" title="Income disparity">socioeconomic disparity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">juvenile delinquency</a>, and drug addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Senegal is a major recipient of international development assistance. Donors include the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> (USAID), Japan, France and China. Over 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> Volunteers have served in Senegal since 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-pcsenegal.org_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcsenegal.org-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Senegal" title="Agriculture in Senegal">Agriculture in Senegal</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Agriculture_in_Senegal&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cowpea_vendors_Thies_Senegal_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cowpea_vendors_Thies_Senegal_2008.jpg/300px-Cowpea_vendors_Thies_Senegal_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/Cowpea_vendors_Thies_Senegal_2008.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="268"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Cowpea_vendors_Thies_Senegal_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Cowpea vendors near Thies, Senegal.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> 
        <p>Agriculture is one of the dominant parts of <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Senegal" title="Economy of Senegal">Senegal's economy</a>. Even though Senegal lies within the drought-prone <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> region, only about 5 percent of the land <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigated</a>, thus Senegal continues to rely on rain-fed agriculture. Agriculture occupies about 75 percent of the workforce. Despite a relatively wide variety of agricultural production, the majority of farmers produce for <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence</a> needs. <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">Millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> are the primary food crops grown in Senegal. Production is subject to drought and threats of <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Locusts" class="mw-redirect" title="Locusts">locusts</a>, birds, <a href="/wiki/Tephritidae" title="Tephritidae">fruit flies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_flies" class="mw-redirect" title="White flies">white flies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas-74">[74]</a></sup> Moreover, the <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Senegal" title="Climate change in Senegal">effects of climate change in Senegal</a> are expected to severely harm the agricultural economy due to <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> such as drought, as well as increased temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_in_Senegal_:0-Sen_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_in_Senegal_:0-Sen-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
        <p>Senegal is a net food importer, particularly for rice, which represents almost 75 percent of cereal imports. <a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> are important <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash crops">cash crops</a>, and a wide variety of fruits and vegetables are grown for local and export markets. In 2006 <a href="/wiki/Gum_arabic" title="Gum arabic">gum arabic</a> exports soared to $280 million, making it by far the leading agricultural export. <a href="/wiki/Green_beans" class="mw-redirect" title="Green beans">Green beans</a>, industrial <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherry_tomato" title="Cherry tomato">cherry tomato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">melon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a> are Senegal's main vegetable cash crops. The <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">Casamance</a> region, isolated from the rest of Senegal by <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a>, is an important agriculture producing area, but without the infrastructure or <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Senegal" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Senegal">transportation</a> links to improve its capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> Despite the lack of modernization of <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_fishing" title="Artisanal fishing">artisanal fishing</a>, the fishing sector remains Senegal's main economic resource and major foreign exchange earner. The livestock and poultry sectors are relatively underdeveloped and have potential for modernization, development and growth. Senegal imports most of its milk and dairy products. The sector is inhibited due to low output and limited investments. The potential production of fauna and forest products is high and diversified and could, if well organized, benefit poor farmers in rural areas. Although the agricultural sector was impacted by a locust invasion in 2004, it has recovered and gross agricultural production is expected to increase by 6 percent in 2006 and 5 percent in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_in_Senegal_fas-74">[74]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">Fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20130513-DSC_8564_(8750149526).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/220px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/330px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/440px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20130513-DSC_8564_(8750149526).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fishing boats in Dakar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Senegal has a 12-nautical-mile (22&nbsp;km; 14&nbsp;mi) exclusive fishing zone that has been regularly breached in recent years (as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>). It has been estimated that the country's fishermen lose 300,000 tonnes of fish each year to <a href="/wiki/Illegal_fishing" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal fishing">illegal fishing</a>. The Senegalese government have tried to control the illegal fishing which is conducted by <a href="/wiki/Fishing_trawlers" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishing trawlers">fishing trawlers</a>, some of which are registered in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. In January 2014, a Russian trawler, <i>Oleg Naydenov</i>, was seized by Senegalese authorities close to the maritime border with <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Senegal" title="Energy in Senegal">Energy in Senegal</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Energy_in_Senegal&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <div class="thumb tright">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_electricity_production.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Senegal_electricity_production.svg/400px-Senegal_electricity_production.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Senegal_electricity_production.svg/600px-Senegal_electricity_production.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Senegal_electricity_production.svg/800px-Senegal_electricity_production.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="585"></a> 
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Senegal_electricity_production.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
           </div>Senegal electricity production by source
          </div>
         </div>
        </div> 
        <p>As of April&nbsp;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Senegal" title="Energy in Senegal">energy sector in Senegal</a> has an installed capacity of 1431&nbsp;megawatts (MW).<sup id="cite_ref-Energy_in_Senegal_:0_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_in_Senegal_:0-77">[77]</a></sup> Energy is produced by private operators and sold to the <a href="/wiki/Senelec" title="Senelec">Senelec</a> energy corporation. According to a 2020 report by the International Energy Agency, Senegal had nearly 70% of the country connected to the national grid.<sup id="cite_ref-Energy_in_Senegal_:1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_in_Senegal_:1-78">[78]</a></sup> Current government strategies for electrification include investments in off-grid solar and connection to the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-Energy_in_Senegal_:0_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_in_Senegal_:0-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Energy_in_Senegal_:1_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_in_Senegal_:1-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
